Educational Tidbits

Director of the Jiangsu Education Department Zhou Fohai

Letter to Secondary School Principals

Discussing Training, Teaching and Administrative Issues

Zhou Fohai, Director of the Jiangsu Education Department, sent a letter to the principals of secondary schools yesterday, saying:

Jiangsu Province's education has always enjoyed a high reputation. Since I was ordered to oversee education in this province, I have deeply feared that the reality will not live up to the name, thus failing the public's expectations. Therefore, I have been diligently working day and night, daring not to be idle. Fortunately, with the efforts of my colleagues, secondary education in the province has been put on the right track, and the studies of young people have been spared from neglect. Looking back on myself, I am somewhat comforted. However, educational undertakings either advance or retreat. Although the progress of secondary education in Jiangsu Province can be said to be step by step, and past achievements can be seen, if we take the entire education as a comprehensive calculation, then the joint efforts of Fohai and my colleagues over the years are still just patching up the gaps. Although there is also the reality of reforming the old and establishing the new, the work of patching up has not been completed for a day, and the foundation of innovation has not been established for a day. Therefore, looking forward to the future, I am both happy and afraid. I am happy that the vitality of the principals and colleagues can last for a long time without being discouraged, and I am afraid that my personal thoughts may be occasionally sparse and incomplete. Therefore, at the beginning of the semester, I want to have a written chat with the principals and colleagues, wanting to use my incomplete thoughts as a small help to learn from others' strengths, and especially hoping that my colleagues, based on their undiminished vitality, will make the determination to move forward bravely.

Regarding training and teaching, there are several points that I want to express my expectations for, such as the issue of physical education, how to make all teachers and students of the school cheer up together and fundamentally break the habit of being weak, how to make the teaching and training integration system increase the efficiency of implementation and not have the feeling that what is seen is not as good as what is heard, how to make all teachers and students of the school automatically implement the New Life Covenant and not generate the drawbacks of forced whitewashing. For these basic and important issues belonging to the training and teaching aspects, the department will not consider the difficulty of exhausting efforts to plan and launch internally, and especially hopes that the principals and colleagues can also not avoid hard work and complaints to exhaust efforts to implement and promote externally, so that the advocacy of laws and regulations can become the school's atmosphere. In this way, the spirit of the training and teaching aspects of secondary education in the province will rise without being invigorated.

Regarding administration, there are also several matters that are hoped to be implemented diligently, such as how to execute laws and regulations with special speed to make administrative efficiency increase exceptionally, how to audit in advance when going out on official business to save time, how to pay attention to full-time employment and reduce part-time positions when hiring teachers without losing the reality of choosing people for the job, how to not slightly exist the habit of being lenient or perfunctory due to the friendship of colleagues and the habits of senior students when handling training and teaching matters, how to try to avoid dealing with the external environment to make the spirit of running the school be single-minded and not divided, how to carry forward the inherent spirit of seeking truth from facts in various schools so that the publication of any publication not only has no smell of propaganda text but also has the spirit of cherishing people's strengths. All of these are just what Fohai has thought of personally, thinking that they are more important in the school's administration. It is not necessarily that the principals and colleagues do not pay attention to them on weekdays, but it is hoped that all colleagues will pay special attention to them in the future. For the key to governance is not in saying more, but in acting vigorously. If the work is not vigorously implemented in various schools, then any plans of the Education Department are just empty words.

In short, Fohai has been with the principals and colleagues for a long time. We treat each other with sincerity and understand each other with impartiality. There is nothing that cannot be said, and everything can be said. The suggestions made by the principals and colleagues on weekdays have made Fohai deeply benefit from collecting opinions, and the temporary speeches of Fohai may also be a resource for the colleagues to learn from. We hope to work together to use the spirit of reforming the old and establishing the new to do the work of making up for the deficiencies. The day when the work of making up for the deficiencies is completed is the time when the foundation of innovation is established. I would like to encourage all my colleagues. Words cannot express everything. I hope you will understand.

Autumn Seasonal Foods 32

— Zhu Yun

Although the weather is still arid, several showers have brought a touch of coolness to the mornings and evenings. The autumn wind rustles, the earth is already veiled in misty mountains, and the sounds of insects fill the ears. After enduring the scorching summer, people's appetites naturally improve in this cool weather. Moreover, it is the season for spring flowers and autumn fruits; the perch is plump, the crabs are full of roe, the water caltrop is delicious, and the fox nuts are fresh. Various fruits are also in season. Strolling through the markets, the colors of orange, yellow, pear white, red, and purple dazzle the eyes, and one cannot help but be tempted. Therefore, I have selected and recorded some of the seasonal foods of autumn to create a small cookbook.

(1) Dishes

Spring Chicken These days, chickens are not yet large and robust, but their feathers are full, and they have lost their chick-like appearance. This type of chicken is like a young person, full of vitality. The chicken meat is tender and melts in the mouth. When braised until tender, even the bones are tender enough to chew. The flavor is especially rich and delicious, and it is also highly nutritious. Whether boiled or braised, it is endlessly flavorful. If simmered into chicken broth, it is also an excellent tonic!

Crab Crabs are a seasonal delicacy in autumn, as famous in Jiangnan as the perch of Songjiang. They scuttle sideways on the banks of lakes where reeds and knotweed grow. The Yangcheng Lake in Suzhou is famous for its crabs. These crabs have golden yellow hairs on their claws and strong claws that can stand and move sideways on a lacquered table, hence the name "Golden Claw Yangcheng". Unfortunately, this year's drought has caused significant drying of Yangcheng Lake, which will inevitably affect crab production. In addition to steaming and enjoying them with ginger and vinegar, crabs can also be cooked with flour or stir-fried with crab meat (crab roe), both of which are excellent autumn dishes. In addition to stir-frying, crab roe can also be used as a filling for various dim sum with pork and shrimp, with a fresh and delicious taste.

(2) Fruits

Apples These days, apples and pears are the most affordable fruits and are very common. Their bright red color resembles the rouge on a girl's face, making them very attractive. Apples can not only aid digestion but also prevent illness. A Western proverb says, "An apple a day keeps the doctor away." Ancient Chinese prescriptions say that apples can treat dysentery, and modern Western medicine has also proven that apple powder is highly effective in treating dysentery, demonstrating that apples have disease-curing effects in addition to aiding digestion.

Grapes Grapes contain a large amount of iron and have the effect of strengthening the stomach and body. Their shape resembles purple crystal balls, clear and lovely. Wine is undoubtedly an excellent drink, and grape juice is also fresh and sweet. Unfortunately, our country pays too little attention to the cultivation of grapes, so that the bunches of grapes in fruit shops are almost entirely imported. In this year of sharply increasing imports, it is truly alarming to see the state of our domestic products.

Water Caltrop The water caltrop from Suzhou is very famous, with many varieties successively appearing on the market. From early autumn to late autumn, water caltrop is continuously available. There are five types of water caltrop in Suzhou: small ones include acute-angled water caltrop and round-angled water caltrop, and large ones include small white water caltrop, monk's water caltrop, and wonton water caltrop. They can be eaten raw or cooked. Wonton water caltrop is especially fragrant and glutinous, making it the best of all water caltrop varieties.

Fox Nut Fox nut is a famous local product of Suzhou. When it is in the water, it is wrapped in its skin and looks like a chicken head, hence its common name "chicken head". The flesh of the chicken head is white and crystalline. The romantic Tang Emperor, Tang Xuanzong, stroked Consort Yang's nipples and called them "freshly peeled chicken head meat", which shows how lovely the shape of fox nut is. Fox nut soup is fragrant and delicious. Ground into a paste and cooked, it is also sweet and fragrant, making it a unique nourishing food for the elderly.

Chestnuts and Ginkgo Chestnuts have just come on the market these days. Stalls selling sugar-roasted chestnuts can be found everywhere in the market. These chestnuts are fragrant, glutinous, and sweet. Chewing on them in one's leisure time is indeed more substantial than eating melon seeds. In addition to roasting, chestnuts can also be cooked with chicken, which is very flavorful. Although ginkgo has a slightly bitter taste when stir-fried, it is also very delicious when cooked in porridge or stir-fried in dishes.

(3) Pastries

Mooncake It is the seasonal pastry of autumn. Although Suzhou mooncakes are not as huge and expensive as those from Guangdong, they also come in both vegetarian and meat fillings, with sweet and savory flavors, and the fillings number no less than twenty. Among the sweet ones, those with jujube paste, bean paste, rose, and mint are the best. The savory ones are best with fresh meat. When they are baked and come out of the oven, their deliciousness is truly beyond words!

Creation and Time 33

— Huang Huaibai

The completion of a great work requires a considerable amount of time. This is an undeniable fact in history. To cite a few examples:

Zuo Si's "Rhapsody on the Three Capitals" was so widely recited that paper in Luoyang became expensive because he spent ten years writing it. Goethe's poetic drama "Faust" was so revolutionary in the world of literature and is still popular today because he spent fifty years, from the age of twenty-three to eighty-three, completing this masterpiece. Milton's position in English literature is second only to Shakespeare. However, his greatest epic poem, "Paradise Lost," also took twenty-seven years to write. Others, such as Thomson's "The Castle of Indolence" and Hardy's "The Dynasts," took more than ten years to complete. Even the short-lived genius poet Byron, who lived only thirty-six years, spent five years writing his satirical poem called "Don Juan." These are all very obvious facts. From these facts, we can imagine how diligent and careful a great writer is when writing his creation. Then, the honor and price obtained by publishing such works can naturally compensate for the energy and time he has sacrificed. Therefore, the creations that are called great writers are all obtained through long-term effort and hard work. They have their own way to achieve success, and their honors and positions are not obtained by luck or accident. Understanding this, we can confidently say that the quality of creation is directly proportional to time.

Of course, it is not difficult to find a few writers with quick wit and talent in history, such as Cao Zhi and Yuan Hu, one of whom could write poetry in seven steps, and the other could write while leaning on a horse. However, these are special geniuses, one in a hundred years. Educational psychologists tell us that geniuses and the mentally deficient account for a very small number. What nature gives us is mostly mediocre talent. To think of emulating these few special geniuses with mediocre talent is not only counterproductive but also impossible.

However, what is the situation in our current literary world? In terms of quantity, the so-called creations are produced in batches, which is quite impressive. But in terms of quality, except for a very few works that are worth appreciating, most of them are not decent. The writers' desire and courage to create are truly enviable, but their attitude towards creation is too casual. The only reason for this is that they have neglected the time required for creation. In this way, the rate of creation has increased, but the content of creation has undoubtedly been counterproductive. As a result, most of the works circulating in the publishing industry are shoddy. This cannot be solely attributed to the writers themselves. The urging of booksellers and the blind encouragement of critics must also bear considerable responsibility.

Finally, I hope that writers will not cherish time too much. The garden of literature cannot be built in one fell swoop. It takes a lot of time to cultivate. Prolific writers are not what we need now. Great writers are what we really need. Because ten pounds of iron cannot be worth the price of one pound of gold, this is an honest saying.

Beginning and End 34

— Zhou Muzhai

As long as one is not forgetful, one should still remember the resounding slogan of the past: "Catch up from the front!" This was based on one's own backwardness. Let's not worry about whether we caught up or not, but at least we faced the front for a while.

Someone doubted this slogan, saying, "Catching up is to catch up from behind the tail. How can you catch up from the front? Since you are catching up from behind the tail, whether you walk slowly or speed up, you have to catch up step by step. You can't jump."

Listening to this, it seems reasonable, as if the slogan is incomprehensible, but in reality, it is "dissecting the meaning out of context." When you catch up, others are not standing still; they may even be moving faster. If you are behind the tail, assuming the speed is the same, then the tail of others is always your head. Wherever your head is, it is always the tail of others. Catch, catch, catch. How can you catch up? The meaning of "catch up from the front" is nothing more than learning from the progressive things of others, not learning from the dregs that others have abandoned, that is, to catch up from the front, not to chase after the tail. Of course, when catching up from the front, it would be best if you could take a look at the tail. The feces of others may be used as our fertilizer. But fertilizer is just fertilizer. Don't take it as a real meal.

But catching up behind the tail of others is still better than not catching up at all. Because the tail of others is always more advanced than us. It's always better than catching your own tail behind your own tail. Catching your own tail behind your own tail is like a standing dog, not knowing if it's itchy or for some other reason, turning around to bite its own tail, but can't bite it, just spinning around there, only amusing people.

The ancestors of mankind originally had tails. We have a "national curse," and it is an "ancient and strange curse," called "beasts in clothing." Although it is cursing people, although it comes from the mouths of those who do not understand science, it secretly coincides with anthropology. Only because the beasts were clothed did they lose a tail. "Customs" records two idioms: "The fox wants to cross the river, but what about the tail?" This says that the fox is bewildered by the inability to control its tail before crossing the river. The "Book of Changes" says, "The fox's tail is wet with fire." This says that the fox's tail is broken and rotten during the river crossing, and it must be very frustrated. It can be seen how the fox suffered from the loss of its tail, and mankind should be grateful for its fortune.

Should the Twenty-Four Histories Be Sold as a Complete Set? 35

— Pei Wei

In Mr. Lingmo's article "Starting from the Twenty-Four Histories" published in Free Talk a few days ago, he mentioned Kaiming's Twenty-Five Histories; and proposed revising the Twenty-Four Histories and publishing them in categories.

I generally agree with Mr. Lingmo's opinion: but I think there is room for discussion regarding his statement that "the Twenty-Four Histories should not be sold as a complete set at all."

Why shouldn't the Twenty-Four Histories be sold as a complete set at all? Mr. Lingmo offers two reasons: (1) Those who specialize in studying various aspects of a certain dynasty only need the history books of that dynasty and the two dynasties before and after it, so selling the Twenty-Four Histories as a complete set is extremely uneconomical for readers. (2) Those who specialize in studying a certain aspect of each dynasty need a certain part of each history, so for the convenience of readers, the Twenty-Four Histories should be published in categories, and should not be sold as a complete set. Regarding the first point, I think that Mr. Lingmo overemphasizes the change of dynasties of one surname and one family. In fact, history is continuous. The change of dynasties is only the transfer of political power. All systems and cultures have their relationship of inheriting the past and paving the way for the future. Therefore, to study the system and culture of a certain dynasty, one must first have a bird's-eye view of the history of the past five thousand years. Just as if we want to study the land equalization system of the Later Wei Dynasty, we must trace it back to the ancient well-field system, and even more, we must clarify the situation of powerful families annexing land since the Qin and Han Dynasties. At the same time, we must also study how the land equalization system affected later generations. In this way, what he needs is not only "the history books of a certain dynasty and the two dynasties before and after it." Regarding the second point, I also agree with Mr. Lingmo's proposal to publish in categories; but I think that publishing in categories and selling as a complete set can proceed in parallel. After all, the Twenty-Four Histories are different from ordinary encyclopedias. To study a certain aspect of each dynasty, what we need is not only a certain part of each history. For example, the treatises on astronomy and the five elements in the Twenty-Four Histories, although they are a part that "ordinary readers cannot read or do not need to read," but if we want to study the religious thought of feudal society, the treatises on astronomy and the five elements are excellent reference materials. Not only that, if we want to study the economic policies and land systems of past dynasties, the treatises on food and goods in each history are naturally excellent materials, but some historical materials have to be found outside of the treatises on food and goods. Just as the Treatise on Food and Goods in the Book of Han says, "Duke Xiao of Qin used Shang Yang, destroyed the merged fields, opened up fields, and emphasized the rewards of farming and warfare, ... so he overthrew neighboring countries and became a hegemon among the feudal lords." What was the effect of Shang Yang's changing the field system at that time, whether productivity was improved, and why destroying the well-field system and opening up fields would overthrow neighboring countries and make him a hegemon among the feudal lords, the Treatise on Food and Goods in the Book of Han does not clearly tell us; so we have to turn to the Biography of Shang Yang in the Records of the Grand Historian, which tells us that after Shang Yang changed the field system, "every household was rich and people were content," and also said that "after ten years of implementation, the villages and towns were greatly governed." We can also find evidence from other biographies, such as the Biography of Li Si in the Records of the Grand Historian, which has the words "Duke Xiao used Shang Yang's laws to change customs, the people became prosperous, and the country became rich and strong." The era of Li Si was not far from Shang Yang, and it can be used as strong corroborating evidence. Therefore, although publishing the Twenty-Four Histories in categories has its conveniences: but if readers only look for a certain type of material from a certain category, they will inevitably miss many important historical materials.

In addition, Mr. Lingmo also proposed that the imperial chronicles and biographies of each history should be arranged according to surnames, and a comprehensive dictionary of personal names should be compiled. The foreign biographies, biographies of the four barbarians, biographies of the Xiongnu, and biographies of the Western Regions in each history should be compiled into a special volume. I think that instead of rearranging the imperial chronicles and biographies of each history according to the number of strokes, it would be more meaningful to make a complete "Index of Personal Names in the Twenty-Four Histories" (the existing "Historical Surname Rhyme Compilation" only lists the names of those who have biographies in history, or those who are relatively famous even without biographies, which is less than one-tenth of the entire history, and there is a need to recompile it, but this work is too large, and it will take ten or five years). As for compiling the Biography of the Xiongnu and the Biography of the Western Regions into a special volume, it may not be an economical method; but if we only read the Biography of the Western Regions of the two Han Dynasties without reading the Biography of Zhang Qian and the Biography of Ban Chao, we still do not have enough understanding of the communication between the Han Dynasty and the Western Regions.

In short, I do not oppose Mr. Lingmo's proposal of categorizing and revising, but I think that the Twenty-Four Histories are fundamentally different from ordinary encyclopedias. The imperial chronicles, tables, treatises, and biographies all have their intricate and interconnected relationships. Although "categorized publishing does not harm the essence of the original book," the complete set of the Twenty-Four Histories has its own value and needs, and it is definitely not "should not be sold as a complete set at all."

Midstream 36

— TK

Memories of Langzhong (Part 2) 37

— Chuan Ren

We have to take an hour here to do the elegant deeds of literati and poets, quietly appreciating Lang Mountain and Lang River, and looking at the fairy buildings of Langyuan. But thinking carefully, the hairs on my body stand on end! In this day and age, we are still learning to dream like idiots and linger on the scenery. I'm afraid that even Lu Dongbin, who writes poetry with cantaloupe juice, is a bit unaccustomed!

According to the stone tablet on Jinping Mountain with Lu Zu's cantaloupe skin poem, it says that Lu Xian visited Junping here, using cantaloupe skin as a pen and cantaloupe juice as ink, and recited poetry on the stone. Later, good people carved the words according to the original trace. The poem says: "When the sea is calm and the river is clear, I ride a deer down from the emerald platform. Just because Junping goes to the bottom of the river, it doesn't hurt to come to Jinping!"

This shows that Lu Zu wants to write poetry and visit friends when the sea is calm and the river is clear. How dare we come here presumptuously on a day when the sea is not calm and the river is not clear? Therefore, poetry grace is not at home this day, and not a single sentence is written, and the reason is not for anything else.

Inside the city, there are refugee camps everywhere. All the ancestral halls and temples are filled with refugees from Tongjiang, Najiang, Bazhong, and other counties. On the one hand, the government provides two meals of porridge a day, and on the other hand, private families cook some black rice themselves. Life is maintained like this. Fortunately, there is no need to work, and the days can be spent for the time being. As for the filth and stench in the camp and the spread of disease, the officials and the people do not care. The local Langzhong people, although their eyes are red with envy at the refugees eating white rice, are helpless, because they supply the government, and the government supplies the refugees. It is originally a heaven and earth of impartiality, benevolence, and righteousness. Can other things still be taken care of?

One morning, I was drinking tea in a small teahouse and talking about the commercial depression. An old man with a dry tobacco pipe walked up to me, dipped his finger in the teacup, and drew the characters "Luo", "Zheng", and "Fa" on the table. His intention was to say that the Luo surname was conquering too much. Although I understood the general idea, I still wanted to ask further, but he stuck out his tongue, turned around, and left!

While I was calming my mind, suddenly someone with a pistol walked by on the street, followed by a red-faced, western-dressed, leather-shoed military officer striding forward. Unexpectedly, an old woman sprang out from the side, knelt forward on both knees, and shouted, "Commander, save me!" The officer glanced at her and immediately called to the guards behind him, "Arrest her!" In this way, he still walked away unconsciously.

Mr. Village Chief (Part 3) 38

— Wang Renshu

"What's wrong! Are you crazy?" followed by the weeping voice of Sister-in-law Wen.

"I'm not crazy, but you are crazy, how can you not even see your husband, and not even tea?"

"Oh! Are you angry with me for this?" This time, Sister-in-law Wen sat down on the bamboo chair. "That's good, that's good, as long as you can provide us with three meals a day, and I don't have to go east and west to beg for favors, I will wait on you with tea all day long! You are a man after all, how can you not even fill the rice bowls of your wife and children, —— you headless corpse! You shameless floater! What kind of bird village chief are you anyway!..."

At this point, Sister-in-law Wen was crying, scolding, and recounting. When she was heartbroken, tears fell like a tide.

"Damn it —— damn it ——"

Under the attack of Sister-in-law Wen, who turned defense into offense, Mr. Feng Wen had to change his tactics and turn attack into defense. He also lowered his voice and used this set of national curses to extricate himself. However, Sister-in-law Wen did not let him go.

"You also have a face. You post notices all day long, run to the district office, climb mountain tops, and you only have enough food for yourself, and you still want the old woman to find a way. Good, if you can kick, then let the old woman go out and see if the old woman can't feed this pus bag that my parents gave me. You headless corpse! You! You!..."

Sister-in-law Wen leaned forward and backward, bouncing on the bamboo chair, which cried out fiercely as if it could not hold her. Mr. Feng Wen knew that he had encountered bad luck today. So he gave up the national curse tactic, picked a fair criticism, and shouted "Shrew! Shrew!" while turning his head and sending his two feet to the aisle.

The son, Rugang, was like a little mud pig, rolling around on the street. His black face was groping and picking things, as if he found it very interesting. Probably, he didn't know that he was the son of a village chief! What an unlucky year!

He stood in the street in front of the door for a while, and when he heard the crying inside the house subside, he felt a little more at ease.

"Damn it, there's really nothing to say!" This time, Mr. Feng Wen shot a cold arrow at his own heart. "Isn't it true that you're worried about starving to death even if you're a village chief? What kind of world is this?"

Thinking about it, he turned his eyes to the street.

Elaboration on Treating Typhoid Fever 4 (The Greater Yang Stage) (Part 2) 40

— Yu Yunzhou

Cinnamon Twig Decoction (Gui Zhi Tang) can induce sweating. Although this is not explicitly stated in the original scripture, it is mentioned in other records. Moreover, it is evident in Zhang Zhongjing's writings, as the instances of using Cinnamon Twig Decoction to induce sweating are numerous. For example, in the upper section of the Greater Yang Stage, it says, "If after taking Cinnamon Twig Decoction, profuse sweating occurs, and the pulse is surging and large, administer Cinnamon Twig Decoction again according to the previous method." It also says, "If after taking Cinnamon Twig Decoction, profuse sweating occurs, followed by great thirst that cannot be relieved, and the pulse is surging and large, administer White Tiger Decoction with Ginseng." These all indicate that Cinnamon Twig Decoction causes profuse sweating, meaning it not only induces sweating but also induces profuse sweating. This is the "like water flowing away" effect mentioned in the instructions for taking Cinnamon Twig Decoction.

Furthermore, in the middle section of the Greater Yang Stage, it says, "If the external symptoms of Greater Yang disease have not been resolved, and the pulse is floating and weak, sweating should be induced to resolve it. Cinnamon Twig Decoction is appropriate." It also says, "If the patient often sweats spontaneously, this is because the Nutritive Qi (Rong Qi) is harmonious. When the Nutritive Qi is harmonious, there is disharmony externally, because the Defensive Qi (Wei Qi) is not in harmony with the Nutritive Qi... Induce sweating again, and when the Nutritive and Defensive Qi are harmonized, the condition will be cured. Cinnamon Twig Decoction is appropriate." It also says, "If the patient has no other underlying illness, but experiences intermittent fever and spontaneous sweating that does not resolve, this is due to disharmony of the Defensive Qi. Induce sweating before the fever occurs, and the condition will be cured. Cinnamon Twig Decoction is appropriate." It also says, "If, in typhoid fever, there has been no bowel movement for six or seven days, and there is headache and fever, administer Purgative Decoction (Cheng Qi Tang). If the urine is clear, it indicates that the condition is not internal but remains external. Sweating must be induced. If there is headache, there will be bleeding from the nose. Cinnamon Twig Decoction is appropriate." It also says, "If, in typhoid fever, sweating has resolved the condition, but after about half a day, irritability returns, and the pulse is floating and rapid, sweating can be induced again. Cinnamon Twig Decoction is appropriate."

In the Yang Brightness Stage section, it says, "In Yang Brightness disease, if the pulse is slow, there is profuse sweating, and slight aversion to cold, the exterior has not been resolved. Sweating can be induced. Cinnamon Twig Decoction is appropriate." It also says, "If the patient is irritable and feverish, and sweating resolves the condition, and the fever occurs at dusk, resembling malaria, it belongs to the Yang Brightness Stage. If the pulse is solid, purgation is appropriate; if the pulse is floating and empty, sweating is appropriate. Purgation should be done with Purgative Decoction, and sweating should be induced with Cinnamon Twig Decoction."

In the Greater Yin Stage section, it says, "In Greater Yin disease, if the pulse is floating, sweating can be induced. Cinnamon Twig Decoction is appropriate." These are all explicit statements by Zhang Zhongjing regarding the use of Cinnamon Twig Decoction to induce sweating.

Furthermore, at the end of the upper section of the Greater Yang Stage, there is the phrase "increase cinnamon to induce sweating." In the middle section of the Greater Yang Stage, the modifications to Minor Bupleurum Decoction state, "If there is no thirst and slight fever externally, remove ginseng and add three ounces of cinnamon. Cover warmly to induce slight sweating, and the condition will be cured." This is an explicit statement about increasing cinnamon to induce sweating.

However, in the Treatise on Cold Damage, there are also passages such as Cinnamon Twig Decoction with Aconite is used for incessant sweating after inducing sweating, Cinnamon Twig and Licorice Decoction is used for excessive sweating, and Cinnamon Twig and Two Parts Ogre Food Decoction One Part Ephedra Decoction is used when Yang Qi is insufficient and sweating should not be induced. Consequently, there is doubt whether cinnamon is a sweating-inducing herb. Therefore, Wang Haizang believed that cinnamon could neither open the pores to release sweat nor close the sweat pores, attributing its function to harmonizing the Nutritive and Defensive Qi. If the Nutritive and Defensive Qi themselves are not clearly understood and defined, the notion of harmonizing them becomes even more elusive. How audacious the old physicians were to fabricate such absurdities! However, this is not Haizang's fault but Zhongjing's. Zhang Zhongjing's Treatise on Cold Damage contains many contradictory statements.

Regarding the Nutritive and Defensive Qi, in the middle section of the Greater Yang Stage, it says, "If the patient often sweats spontaneously, this is because the Nutritive Qi is harmonious. When the Nutritive Qi is harmonious, there is disharmony externally, because the Defensive Qi is not in harmony with the Nutritive Qi... Induce sweating again, and when the Nutritive and Defensive Qi are harmonized, the condition will be cured. Cinnamon Twig Decoction is appropriate." It also says, "If the patient has no other underlying illness, but experiences intermittent fever and spontaneous sweating that does not resolve, this is due to disharmony of the Defensive Qi. Induce sweating before the fever occurs, and the condition will be cured. Cinnamon Twig Decoction is appropriate." This suggests that spontaneous sweating indicates harmonious Nutritive Qi and disharmonious Defensive Qi, and that inducing sweating harmonizes the Defensive Qi. The Nutritive Qi is inherently harmonious, so there is no need for harmonization.

In the upper section of the Greater Yang Stage, it says, "In Greater Yang Wind-Strike, the Yang is floating and the Yin is weak. Floating Yang causes fever, and weak Yin causes spontaneous sweating." This suggests that spontaneous sweating indicates weak Yin. In old medical books, the terms "Yin" and "Yang" are used very broadly, sometimes referring to blood and Qi, Nutritive and Defensive Qi, and sometimes referring to the pulse. In this passage, "Yin" and "Yang" refer to the pulse, which also implies referring to the Nutritive Qi or blood. How do we know this? Because this passage contrasts "weak" with "floating," and floating is a pulse sign, indicating that weak is also a pulse sign.

However, in the middle section of the Greater Yang Stage, it says, "If purgation is performed and the patient experiences heaviness in the body and palpitations, sweating should not be induced. Spontaneous sweating should occur to resolve the condition. The reason is that the cubit pulse is weak, indicating internal deficiency. The exterior and interior must be substantial, and the fluids will naturally harmonize, leading to spontaneous sweating and recovery." It also says, "If the cubit pulse is slow, sweating should not be induced. How do we know this? Because the Nutritive Qi is insufficient, and there is a deficiency of blood." Observing these two passages, we know that sweating should not be induced because the cubit pulse is weak and slow. The reason is attributed to internal deficiency and insufficient Nutritive Qi, further explained as a deficiency of blood. Therefore, what is meant by "internal deficiency" is nothing more than insufficient Nutritive Qi, or, in essence, a deficiency of blood.

Furthermore, in the upper section of the Greater Yang Stage, it says, "If the pulse is weak and there is aversion to cold, this indicates that both Yin and Yang are deficient, and sweating, vomiting, or purgation should not be induced again." Cheng Wuji's commentary states, "Yang refers to the exterior, and Yin refers to the interior. A weak pulse indicates internal deficiency, and aversion to cold indicates external deficiency." Therefore, a weak pulse and internal deficiency are synonymous with Yin deficiency and Yin weakness, which also means insufficient Nutritive Qi and a deficiency of blood.

In the middle section of the Greater Yang Stage, it says, "In Greater Yang disease, if there is fever and sweating, this indicates that the Nutritive Qi is weak and the Defensive Qi is strong, causing sweating. To alleviate the pathogenic wind, Cinnamon Twig Decoction is appropriate." This indicates that weak Yin is equivalent to weak Nutritive Qi. Therefore, I say that the Yin and Yang in the previous passage refer to the pulse, but also to Qi and blood, Nutritive and Defensive Qi. The so-called Yin is the Nutritive Qi. However, observing Zhang Zhongjing's writings, it says, "Weak Yin causes spontaneous sweating," and "Spontaneous sweating indicates that the Nutritive Qi is harmonious." Xu Huixi states, "Harmonious Nutritive Qi means the Nutritive Qi is not diseased." If weak Yin means insufficient Nutritive Qi, then does insufficient Nutritive Qi mean that the Nutritive Qi is not diseased? This is a contradiction in the Treatise on Cold Damage regarding the Nutritive and Defensive Qi.

Regarding the use of cinnamon, in the upper section of the Greater Yang Stage, it says, "Cinnamon is primarily for resolving the muscles. If the person has a floating and tight pulse, fever, and no sweating, it should not be administered. This must always be recognized and not mistakenly used." This indicates that cinnamon should not be used without sweating, a profound warning. However, in the instructions for Cinnamon Twig Decoction, it says, "It is even better if the entire body feels warm and there is a slight hint of sweat." This means that even the slightest hint of sweat is absent before taking the decoction. I do not know if the so-called spontaneous sweating is even slighter than the slightest hint of sweat. It also says, "If there is no sweating, take it again according to the previous method. If there is still no sweating, take the next dose sooner." It also says, "If sweating does not occur, take up to two or three doses." I do not know how to differentiate the absence of sweating that contraindicates the use of Cinnamon Twig Decoction from the absence of sweating that requires taking two or three doses.

Furthermore, in the middle section of the Greater Yang Stage, it says, "After inducing sweating, Cinnamon Twig Decoction should not be administered again. If there is sweating and wheezing without high fever, Ephedra, Apricot Kernel, Licorice, and Gypsum Decoction can be administered." Ke Yunbo states, "Zhang Zhongjing often uses Cinnamon Twig Decoction to induce sweating again when the exterior is not resolved after sweating or purgation." He also says, "Administering Cinnamon Twig Decoction again when the exterior is not resolved after sweating or purgation is a common method for treating wind-cold." From this, it can be seen that the statement "After inducing sweating, Cinnamon Twig Decoction should not be administered again" is contradictory. If it is because of wheezing, then thickening the Cinnamon Twig Decoction and adding Magnolia Bark and Apricot Kernel is appropriate. If it is because of sweating, then Cinnamon Twig Decoction should be used. Why abandon cinnamon and use ephedra? If it is because there is no high fever, why use gypsum? These are all based on old theories and are not understandable. Therefore, Ke changed "sweating and wheezing" to "no sweating and wheezing" to align with the ephedra in the formula and changed "no high fever" to "high fever" to align with the gypsum in the formula. Although his explanation is not entirely accurate, he recognizes that it is not understandable. Chen Xiuyuan claimed that the wheezing is the wheezing characteristic of ephedra's indication, that sweating is the absence of sweating characteristic of ephedra's indication, and that the absence of high fever is because the heat is suppressed internally, rising to the surface, making the external heat appear lighter. Although his explanation is also not entirely accurate, he recognizes that it is not understandable. However, although there are many explanations, none can be found that are entirely without regrets. This is simply because Zhongjing himself is contradictory, and later scholars cannot rectify it. Zhongjing's writings contain many contradictions, and they are especially prominent in the discussion of Cinnamon Twig Decoction. Yan Jing Liao Ping even suggests that Cinnamon Twig Decoction is not a single formula but that there must be several formulas with the same name, similar to how Purgative Decoction has Major Purgative Decoction, Minor Purgative Decoction, and Stomach-Regulating Purgative Decoction. Therefore, he gathered nineteen formulas from the Golden Mirror of Medical Prescriptions, such as Four-Ingredient Cinnamon Twig Decoction and Five-Ingredient Cinnamon Twig Decoction, to support this claim, believing that this would clarify the explanation of Cinnamon Twig Decoction. Although his theory is novel, unless we could revive Zhang Zhongjing and ask him, who could believe whether it is true or not?

Relapsing Fever 41

— Yizhi

Recently, Professor Liu Fu (Bannong) of Peking University passed away due to illness. He died of relapsing fever. When the illness started, he only had some fever. Because there were no testing facilities locally, the cause of his illness could not be determined. It was only after returning to Beiping that relapsing fever was diagnosed, but it was already too late. Many people are blaming new medicine for this, but in reality, it was because there was no new medicine that Mr. Liu was sacrificed. If there had been good testing facilities locally, blood could have been drawn and tested immediately to identify the cause of the illness and provide treatment. Then, would Mr. Liu not still be on the podium at Peking University today? This makes us realize the importance of new medicine, especially the need for new medicine and pharmaceuticals in rural areas. We must recognize that countless others have been sacrificed under similar circumstances. Mr. Liu was just one of them.

Relapsing fever is an acute infectious disease. Its pathogen was discovered in 1873 by Obermeier, and it is a spiral-shaped bacterium. The route of entry into the human body is usually through the bites of mosquitoes, lice, or bedbugs, because these bacteria are often found in the excrement of these insects. After a person is bitten, they scratch the itchy area, and the bacteria enter the body. Furthermore, the saliva, tears, milk, urine, and other secretions of people with relapsing fever also contain the bacteria, making the route of transmission even wider. Air, daily necessities, bedding, and so on can all be mediums of transmission.

After the bacteria enter the body, symptoms appear after about five to eight days. The initial symptoms include headache, back pain, and chills, gradually progressing to body aches. The body temperature rises to 40 to 41 degrees Celsius (102 to 105 degrees Fahrenheit). The temperature fluctuates, but the difference is not significant. Usually, after six or seven days, profuse sweating occurs, and the fever subsides. However, after a few days (approximately four to fourteen days, depending on the case), the same symptoms reappear. After another six or seven days, the fever subsides again. After a few more days, the fever returns, and the cycle repeats. That is why it is called relapsing fever. The second and third occurrences of fever are usually milder than the first. Some people recover on their own after two or three occurrences; otherwise, they may die from heart failure or related lung and liver diseases.

If we encounter such patients, we should immediately test their blood. If they have relapsing fever, the spiral bacteria will be found in their blood.

Currently, the most common treatment method is the injection of Salvarsan (914). Usually, the fever subsides after one injection. In addition, mild symptomatic medications can be used for back pain, headache, vomiting, constipation, and so on, and recovery is easily achieved.

This disease does not confer immunity, so there is still a possibility of a second infection after having it once.

The prevention method lies entirely in public health measures. We should pay attention to those who are ill. Once such a patient is found, immediate measures should be taken to isolate them. All utensils used by the patient should be disinfected immediately. The patient's excrement should not be left exposed. If this is done, the bacteria will have no chance of survival, and mosquitoes and other insects will have nothing to spread.

Common Knowledge Q&A About Diseases 42

— Cheng Hanzhang

(39) Hookworm (also known as Duodenal Worm)

(Q) What kind of worm is a hookworm?

(A) A hookworm is a type of worm that parasitizes the upper part of the small intestine, especially the duodenum, which is where they live. Therefore, it is also known as a duodenal worm.

Page 18

(Q) What does a hookworm look like?

(A) Male hookworms are 10 mm long, and female hookworms are 18 mm long. Their mouths have hooks and teeth that they use to tightly grip the mucous membrane of the intestinal wall to parasitize it.

(Q) What do hookworm eggs look like?

(A) The eggs are oval-shaped, and their contents contain numerous cleavage globules. The eggshell is thin and colorless.

(Q) What symptoms occur after hookworms parasitize the human intestinal tract?

(A) People parasitized by hookworms often develop severe anemia, with symptoms such as general fatigue, headache, rapid heartbeat, dizziness, tinnitus, swollen skin, pale complexion, heart murmurs, and murmurs in the jugular vein.

(Q) Are there any abnormalities in the feces excreted by the patient?

(A) The feces of hookworm patients contain worm eggs, eosinophils, Charcot-Leyden crystals, and occult blood.

(Q) What symptoms does the patient experience?

(A) Patients often complain of thirst, decreased appetite, nausea, abdominal pain, and bloating.

(Q) What are some medications for expelling hookworms?

(A) Carbon tetrachloride, thymol, oil of chenopodium, etc.

(Q) How is carbon tetrachloride used?

(A) On the day before deworming, give the patient some semi-liquid foods such as milk, egg broth, and thin porridge. At 10:00 AM, administer castor oil or magnesium sulfate internally to ensure that the intestines are thoroughly cleansed. On the day of deworming, take 3 cubic centimeters of carbon tetrachloride in capsules in the morning. After two hours, take another 20-30 grams of magnesium sulfate. Continue this for several days to completely expel the worms. Regular food can be eaten as usual and does not need the same attention as on the first day.

(Q) What should be avoided when taking carbon tetrachloride?

(A) Avoid fats and alcohol.

(Q) How is thymol used?

(A) Prepare for deworming the day before using thymol. On the morning of the deworming day, take 4 grams of thymol and 2 grams of naphthalene, divided into two packets. Take the first packet, and two hours later, take castor oil once. After the bowel movement, take the second packet.

(Q) Are there any things to avoid when taking this medication?

(A) Because alcohol dissolves thymol, it should also be avoided.

(Q) How is oil of chenopodium used?

(A) Prepare for deworming the day before. In the morning on an empty stomach, take 20 drops of oil of chenopodium in a capsule, all at once. Two hours later, take castor oil to expel the worms.

Common Knowledge of Ear, Nose, Throat, and Eye Hygiene 43

— Tang Renjin

(15) External Auditory Canal Inflammation (Ear Boil)

External auditory canal inflammation (otitis externa) is one of the most common ear diseases. We often encounter it in our clinical practice, and it is somewhat more common in women. It usually occurs on one side, and rarely on both sides. The main cause is the invasion of pyogenic bacteria (such as staphylococcus) into the sebaceous glands or ceruminous glands of the skin of the external auditory canal. However, the skin of the external auditory canal has its own resistance that can prevent the invasion of pyogenic bacteria. However, this resistance can sometimes weaken or be completely absent. At this time, pyogenic bacteria can invade. There are many reasons for weakened or absent resistance. Usually, it can be divided into: 1. Mechanical irritation, such as scratching the external auditory canal (self-cleaning with ear picks or barbers using small knives to scrape the ear, etc.). 2. Chemical and thermal irritation. 3. Irritation from pus draining from suppurative otitis media. 4. Unclean water entering the ear during swimming.

The main symptom of this disease is usually the onset of ear pain. Ear pain is usually more severe at night than during the day, and can even interfere with sleep. The pain is more severe if the earlobe is pulled or the outer opening of the ear is pressed. Sometimes, it feels difficult to open the mouth and inconvenient to chew. At this time, if the external auditory canal is examined with an otoscope, localized tenderness and redness and swelling of the affected area can often be detected. The patient often has fever and listlessness. If the swelling increases, the external auditory canal can be completely blocked, thus hindering hearing. At the same time, the area in front of or behind the ear often becomes red and swollen, and may even suppurate.

The course of this disease is about one week, but it is easily recurring. It can often develop into diffuse external auditory canal inflammation (otitis externa diffusa). At this time, the wall of the external auditory canal is particularly red and swollen. First, the epidermis peels off, and then ulcers form. The surface is very moist, and the secretion is serous or purulent, often mixed with exfoliated epidermal cells and earwax, forming a dirty, muddy substance with a foul odor. Secretion stops only when healing is imminent. The skin surface of the external auditory canal gradually dries.

The most important prevention method for external auditory canal inflammation is to prevent the invasion of pyogenic bacteria. Avoid irritation of the external auditory canal (abandon the habit of indiscriminate ear picking). Pay attention to the intrusion of dirty water into the ear. If suppurative otitis media already exists, it should be treated immediately to eliminate the pus. If the external auditory canal ever feels painful and swollen, it should be diagnosed and treated by a specialist immediately.

Physician's Code of Conduct of the Chinese Medical Association 44

Duties of a Physician

Article 1: A physician's primary objective is to serve the people.

Article 2: A physician's daily life should be moderate, and they must possess sound physical and mental health to perform their duties.

Essentials of Medical Practice

Article 3: Nobility of Medical Practice: Those engaged in medicine should enhance their academic skills, uphold their noble status, and realize their ideals.

Article 4: Foundation of Medical Practice: Physicians should not practice medicine solely based on dogmatic theories, nor should they rely on doctrines contrary to mainstream global medical science.

Article 5: Unnecessary or Improper Surgery

Application of methods in practice must be generally recognized by the medical community. All unnecessary or improper surgeries should not be performed. Permitting, advising, or performing abortions is against medical ethics. However, in special circumstances, after consultation with other physicians of profound scholarship and integrity, if it is deemed necessary to perform surgery to preserve the mother's life, it may be performed.

Article 6: Respect for Chinese Customs: Foreign physicians practicing in China should not offend Chinese customs and the feelings of the people, especially female patients. When performing an autopsy after a patient's death, Chinese law must be followed, obtaining consent from the deceased's family first, and then submitting a request to the local authorities for approval before execution.

Article 7: Physician's Fees: The fees charged by a physician should be based on the prevailing medical rates in their locality. Remuneration and proper treatment of the patient are two separate issues and should not be intertwined. In particular, one should not sacrifice professional standing or violate public interest due to remuneration issues.

Article 8: No Private Sharing of Commissions: Giving or receiving commissions is detrimental to public interest and degrades the medical profession, which is incompatible with professional ethics. In the event of consultations or surgical treatments, unless the patient or their friends understand the conditions of the agreement, any mutual sharing of commissions is also incompatible with professional ethics.

Article 9: Advertising: Publishing leaflets or advertisements, or using solicitation or interviews to attract patients, is incompatible with professional ethics. Even indirect publicity through referrals or exaggerated claims of therapeutic efficacy in daily newspapers and magazines is also incompatible with professional ethics. Matters such as guaranteeing cures, collecting fees in advance, boasting secret remedies, exaggerating achievements, or using other methods to attract public attention in order to solicit patients are all inappropriate for a physician. However, printing business cards for convenience is a matter of personal preference, and according to local custom, it cannot be considered improper if it is handled appropriately.

Article 10: Secret Remedies and Proprietary Medicines: Using self-prepared medicines

to treat illnesses, or manufacturing, selling, and promoting various self-prepared medicines to profit is incompatible with medical ethics. Receiving a share of profits from patented drugs or various medical and surgical instruments is also incompatible with medical ethics. As for patients bringing prescriptions for dispensing, recommending patients, or submitting specimens for testing, physicians must not secretly receive kickbacks.

Article 11: Certificates: Physicians must not issue false or misleading certificates.

Physician's Responsibility to the Patient

Article 12: Physician's Responsibility: Physicians should not only be prepared to answer a patient's call at any time but also be aware of the nobility of their duty and the weight of their responsibility. During a consultation, they must know that the patient's health and life depend entirely on their skill and proficiency, and they should be extremely cautious and not negligent. For the sake of the patient, they should make every effort to adhere to the scheduled consultation time.

Article 13: Consultation: In the event of difficult or doubtful symptoms, the attending physician should request consultation with other physicians. If the patient or their representative invites other physicians for consultation, the attending physician should also express their agreement.

Article 14: Maintaining Patient's Trust: When diagnosing and treating each patient, one should concentrate their mind and deliberate carefully, maintaining the trust already gained with an attitude of honesty and sincerity. Except as required by law, physicians should not disclose a patient's secrets or speak lavishly of their personal failings or family scandals after a consultation. However, in the case of venereal diseases or other infectious diseases, physicians have a responsibility to protect the patient's family and society from the risk of infection.

Article 15: Treatment of Incurable Diseases: Physicians should not refrain from treating a patient simply because the illness is considered incurable. Treating even when it is known to be incurable aims to reduce the patient's suffering.

Article 16: Obligatory Service: Physicians should recognize that providing medical care to poor patients is a common principle throughout history, both in China and abroad, but this does not apply to foundations, organizations, or life insurance institutions.

Physicians' Right to Receive Free Medical Treatment from Other Physicians

Article 17: Physicians themselves and their immediate family members are entitled to free medical treatment from neighboring physicians. When several physicians treat one person, one of them should preside.

Article 18: When a physician is called to visit a colleague or a colleague's family, the travel expenses and business losses should be borne by the patient's family.

Relationship Between Physicians and Patients Treated by Other Physicians

Article 19: Maintaining Confidentiality in Medical Matters: In ordinary social interactions, physicians should maintain strict confidentiality regarding patients treated by other physicians. It is best not to inquire about the cause of the illness or the state of treatment. Even if there is a desire to inquire, one should not make derogatory insinuations or engage in direct or indirect actions to diminish the patient's faith in their attending physician.

Article 20: Change of Physician: Physicians who are hired to visit a patient already being treated by another physician should not accept the case or prescribe medication, except in the following circumstances: accidental events, the original physician is unwilling to continue treatment, or the patient's family is unwilling to continue engaging the original physician.

Article 21: Appointment of a Substitute: If a physician temporarily leaves due to circumstances, when engaging another physician as a substitute, it should be accepted as a matter of professional courtesy if there is no conflict of interest. After accepting another's appointment, one should do their best to consider the interests and reputation of the one who appointed them and return the patient to them upon their return.

Article 22: Emergencies: When a physician is called for an emergency, either because the family physician cannot arrive in time or because the condition has worsened, their task is limited to providing emergency care. After the family physician arrives, they should inform them of the patient's condition and treatment methods in detail before taking their leave.

Article 23: Obstetric Emergencies: If the originally scheduled obstetrician has not arrived and a visiting physician completes the delivery, the consultation fee should belong to the substituting physician. However, when the originally scheduled physician arrives and with the consent of the family, the substituting physician may respectfully withdraw.

Article 24: Multiple Physicians Invited for Emergencies: In cases of emergency or accidental events, the patient's family often invites several physicians. The invited physicians should advise the patient's family to engage their family physician, and they should take their leave after the family physician arrives.

Consultation

Article 25: Adhering to Consultation Time: Consultation appointments should be strictly adhered to, and one should not break the appointment except in cases of emergency.

Article 26: Consultation Conduct: During consultation, emotions such as vanity, exclusion, and jealousy should be avoided. Due respect should be given to the attending physician, and one should not undermine their credibility with their words.

Article 27: Changes in Treatment Methods: The course of illness is unpredictable, and the attending physician may change their treatment methods without being bound by any prior decision. However, they should explain the reasons for the change at the next consultation. This change can also be made by the consulting physician. The attending physician may prescribe medication for the patient at any time, while the consulting physician may not prescribe medication except in cases of emergency.

Article 28: Disagreement in Diagnosis: If the attending physician and the consulting physician have differing opinions during the diagnosis, another physician should be invited for consultation.

Article 29: Consulting Physician Should Not Accept the Case: Physicians who are invited for consultation should not accept the attending physician's case, even at the request of the patient or their relatives and friends.

Article 30: Referring Patients to Specialists: When the attending physician refers a patient to a specialist, they should attach the medical records. After examination, the specialist should convey their opinion to the attending physician.

Arbitration of Professional Disputes

Article 31: Physicians often have disagreements and conflicts of interest due to differing opinions, leading to disputes. When these cannot be resolved, they should seek arbitration from the medical organization they belong to.

Physicians' Responsibilities to the Nation

Article 32: Assisting in Public Health Undertakings

Physicians consider obedience to laws and respect for social customs as their duty. In order to assist in promoting public health, they should abide by all health regulations.

Article 33: Preventing Infectious Diseases: When needed, physicians should guide patients on quarantine regulations and methods of preventing infectious diseases, and report the infectious diseases they diagnose and treat to the health authorities. In the event of an epidemic, physicians should continue to serve without avoiding danger, with the primary objective of alleviating suffering, even at the risk of their lives.

Article 34: Lawsuits: Regarding lawsuits involving medical matters, physicians should convene a meeting in advance to study the case so that there will be facts to cite in court in the future.

Article 35: Protecting Professional Practice: To protect their professional practice, physicians should avoid cooperating with those of bad character and insufficient knowledge.

Relationship Between Physicians and Nurses

Article 36: Regarding the treatment of diseases or injuries, physicians bear full responsibility, whether in a hospital or clinic. As for the duties of nurses, they should faithfully obey the physician's instructions without discrimination based on the physician's nationality. Nurses must not change the treatment without the physician's permission. Physicians should not be arrogant or unreasonable toward nurses, especially in front of patients.

Conclusion

Article 37: The above sections do not mean that physicians' responsibilities to patients, colleagues, the profession, and the public are limited to these alone, nor does it mean that the scope of medical ethics is limited to this. In short, physicians should treat patients, the public, and their colleagues with a kind attitude at all times, putting themselves in others' shoes and acting with compassion and empathy. The provisions of this article are premised on the interests of the public and will surely gain the sympathy of society.

A Brief Discussion on Pulmonary Tuberculosis (XXI) 45

— Hu Jiayan

What is the condition of hemoptysis in pulmonary tuberculosis? It can occur in any stage of the disease. Its form is individual small streaks of blood, mixed with purulent sputum. Sometimes the quantity is relatively increased, almost several spoonfuls, which is foamy fresh blood, usually expelled after several violent short coughs. In most cases, it can also be about one liter, similar to the situation of stomach bleeding. This kind of massive hemorrhage is only seen in severe cavernous changes and extremely advanced diseases, and its examples are much less than the former. After a patient experiences a bleeding episode, their sputum will also have a slight blood tinge, which gradually decreases and returns to normal after a few days. There are also many examples of repeated hemoptysis. Before these patients experience an episode, they often feel a strange itch in their throat, or even a sweet and bloody smell, which is undoubtedly a precursor. Patients who have experienced repeated hemoptysis are prone to developing severe anemia. After hemoptysis occurs, the temperature may increase, and the pulse rate may also increase. This phenomenon usually gradually decreases after three to five days, which is called hemoptysis (blood heat). However, if the fever persists or even increases significantly, it indicates that the disease is progressing and invading somewhere. Sometimes it can also induce acute miliary tuberculosis. The prognosis in this aspect is certainly not comparable to the former.

The symptom of hemoptysis is easily confused with common hematemesis (i.e., stomach bleeding). In fact, the underlying diseases of these two aspects are completely different. Their simple identification methods are also worth mentioning here. The blood in hemoptysis is bright red, foamy, and does not clot; the blood in hematemesis is dark or black, non-foamy, and often clots into round masses. Hemoptysis is mixed with mucus and pus; hematemesis is mixed with food components. Hemoptysis has an alkaline reaction, and hematemesis has an acidic reaction. Apart from the differences in the discharge itself, the blood in hemoptysis is discharged by coughing, and there are also symptoms of lung and heart disease; the blood in hematemesis is discharged by vomiting, and most have symptoms of stomach and liver disease. These few differences are very obvious, and even the patient themselves can easily distinguish them; however, actual variations are still very common. In cases of massive pulmonary hemorrhage, some blood may also be swallowed and then vomited out again. If the blood stays in the stomach for too long, it can change from bright red and foamy to brown. In this way, it is almost the same as stomach bleeding; not only will the patient misunderstand, but even the doctor may not be able to distinguish it clearly for a while. This completely relies on precise local examinations of these two aspects to reveal the truth.

Apart from pulmonary tuberculosis, other conditions such as lung tumors, pulmonary embolism, heart valve disease, and bronchiectasis can sometimes cause hemoptysis; however, it is far less common than pulmonary tuberculosis. We might as well say that if a patient is found to have hemoptysis, although it is not necessarily pulmonary tuberculosis, it is most likely to be attributed to this disease. As for pulmonary tuberculosis itself, not everyone experiences hemoptysis. According to recent statistics, it is only about a quarter of the number. Among the patients treated by the author, there are many who never experience hemoptysis at all. In the early stages of the disease, hemoptysis occurs in about 10% of cases, and there are many examples where it does not occur a second time. In short, patients who experience hemoptysis are almost all suspected of having pulmonary tuberculosis; however, those who have not experienced it cannot be said not to have pulmonary tuberculosis. This truth should be clearly recognized by everyone.

Page 19

Economic Publication

Remedies for the Dumping of Japanese Aquatic Products 46

— Ruo Qian

The dumping of Japanese aquatic products and the resulting harm to our country's fishing industry have been discussed in previous articles. (See the article "A Review of the Dumping of Japanese Aquatic Products" in this publication.) The only way to prevent it is through tariffs, which is a temporary solution. However, after much struggle, our country has only recently achieved tariff autonomy, and many of the key customs officials are foreigners.

Aquatic products hold an important place in people's diets. Salted and dried fish, in particular, are common among the lower and middle classes, while shark fins and sea cucumbers have, by social convention, become prestigious items for entertaining guests. Domestic production is insufficient, and we rely on foreign goods. Over time, the guest has become the host, and our domestic marine products have gradually declined. Imported marine products have gained an important position in trade, especially those from Japan, which have penetrated every corner. Year after year, the livelihood of coastal fishermen will be completely ruined.

Various tariffs on aquatic products were established in the 6th year of the Xianfeng reign (1856), mostly based on an ad valorem rate of 5%. Even quantitative tariffs were based on this standard. As a result of the Washington Conference, surtaxes were allowed. Later, in the tariff schedules proposed by the Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce, abalone, spiky black sea cucumber, smooth black sea cucumber, white sea cucumber, dried scallops, fish maw, fish spine fins, fish chest fins, shark fins, etc., were all considered luxury goods, with a tax rate of 10%. In the revised tariff schedule of the 11th year of the Republic (1922), the tax rates on aquatic products were also greatly increased. The promulgated national tariff schedule of the 19th year of the Republic (1930) showed even more significant increases. There was another revision in the 22nd year (1933). Now, a table listing the historical tariffs on aquatic products is compiled as follows:

The promulgation of the national tariff schedule in the 19th year (1930) was the result of lifting Japan's obstruction to our country's tariff autonomy and establishing the Sino-Japanese Tariff Reciprocity Agreement. However, in the Sino-Japanese Tariff Reciprocity Agreement, Japan considered China its only export market for aquatic products and insisted on including them in the reciprocity list. As a result, it was stipulated in the second item of the annex, which allowed most of the Japanese aquatic products that were imported in the greatest quantity and caused the greatest pressure to bypass the national tariff schedule through the agreement. Therefore, the import of Japanese aquatic products has been particularly intense in recent years, which needs to be examined. If we compare them, the agreement's tariff rates are much lower than the national tariff rates. Except for unlisted salted fish, kelp threads, and kelp, which are the same, the white sea cucumber is reduced by 46%, and even canned abalone, which is reduced the least, is reduced by 27%. In addition, there are reductions of 42%, 38%, 33%, 31%, 29%, and 28%. If compared with the revised tariff rates of the 22nd year (1933), they are indeed much higher, which can greatly impact Japanese products. The highest is dried scallops, which increased from 9.10 per dan under the agreement's tariff to 29.00 per dan, an actual increase of 218.68%. Even kelp threads, which had the lowest increase, increased by 77%. A table is now presented below to illustrate this.

Comparing the import values, the average monthly import value of Japanese aquatic products during the agreement's tariff period was 19.8% higher than the average monthly import value during the revised tariff schedule period of the 22nd year (1933). (See the article "A Study of the New Customs Import Tariff" in the China Bank Monthly, Volume 9, Issue 2.) If we compare each item (to facilitate comparison, we will examine the total imports of the recent two years, 1932 and 1933), it is even more evident that imports during the agreement period increased much more than after the revision. For example, in 1932, 379,785 dan of kelp were imported, worth 1,151,755 gold units, while in 1931, there were only 195,981 dan, worth 457,053 gold units, a decrease of almost three times. Moreover, the figures for 1933 include a portion of imports still under the agreement's tariff schedule, which shows that the agreement's tariff schedule greatly assisted the import of Japanese aquatic products.
