The above table shows the huge proportion of Japanese products in our country's total aquatic imports. This is because the Japanese took advantage of the agreement's tariffs to import smoothly. Therefore, in the analysis of our country's aquatic import countries, Japanese products outweigh any other country. If we take the average of the import figures during the agreement's tariff period, Japanese products account for 68%. However, during the tariff schedule period of the 22nd year (1933) (until the end of May of the 23rd year (1934)), Japanese products accounted for only 46.5% of the total, which shows that the agreement's tariff schedule favored the import of Japanese products. It also shows that the increase or decrease of aquatic product tariffs is closely related to the import of Japanese products.

Recently, in order to increase revenue, the tariff schedule was re-revised and promulgated on July 1st. In this revised import tariff schedule, the sixth category, fish and shellfish marine products, still has 25 items. Among them, salted sardines, salted salmon, and unlisted salted fish have been changed from quantitative taxes to ad valorem taxes. Abalone, sea cucumber, dried scallops, squid/cuttlefish, kelp threads, kelp, and six other items have had their tax rates reduced. The most significant reduction is for kelp threads in item 292, which has been reduced from 2.30 per 100 kg to 1.70, a decrease of 35.7%. A table listing the tax reductions for several items is shown below:

Item Unit Year 22 Tariff Rate Year 23 Revised Tariff Rate Percentage Reduction from Original Tariff Rate

275 Abalone (A) Loose Per 100 kg 51.00 42.00 21.4%

(B) Canned … 21.00 18.00 16.6

276 Sea Cucumber (A) Spiky Black Sea Cucumber … 51.00 43.00 18.4

(B) Smooth Black Sea Cucumber … 35.00 30.00 16.6

278 Dried Scallops … 48.00 40.00 20.0

282 Squid/Cuttlefish … 17.00 14.00 3.4

292 Kelp Threads … 2.30 1.70 35.2

293 Kelp … 1.70 1.30 30.7

Kelp threads, which have the most significant reduction, had an import value of 1.15 million gold units for 380,000 dan in 1932. In 1933, due to the increased tariff rate, it dropped to 200,000 dan, worth 460,000 gold units. This July (1934), there was a large increase in imports, with over 6,000 dan imported in just one month! This shows the immediate effect! According to historical statistics, Japanese products account for over 99% of all imports. Furthermore, dried scallops account for over 97% of all imports, and abalone accounts for over 70%. Moreover, these abalone, dried scallops, sea cucumbers, and other items are mostly luxury goods, and their purchase elasticity is very strong. If the tax rate is low and the price is cheap, sales will be smooth, and the import of Japanese products will inevitably be high.

Theoretically, China should and can freely increase tariffs. For example, the Tariff Autonomy Act passed in 1925 specifies in the first item of the Tariff Rate Regulations:

"When foreign goods are transported to trading ports in this country, import duties shall be levied in accordance with the taxation methods stipulated in these regulations."

This means that any foreign goods imported should have the obligation to comply with the "taxation methods stipulated" in the Tariff Rate Regulations. Furthermore, in order to protect domestic businesses, the Tariff Rate Regulations also allow for temporary increases in tariffs on foreign goods and stipulate three items: (1) retaliatory tariffs, (2) countervailing tariffs, and (3) anti-dumping tariffs. Currently, Japanese aquatic products are being dumped at reduced prices. Let's look at the provisions of this third item (Article 8 of the original regulations states):

"If foreign goods are intentionally depreciated in price and the government believes that there is a risk of disturbing the market, it may order, in addition to the tax amount listed in the tariff schedule, a tax equivalent to its fair price."

Accordingly, China has the inalienable right to impose appropriate increased taxes on foreign goods that harm our businesses. In the Industrial and Commercial Conference of the 19th year of the Republic (1930), the conditions for preventing dumping through anti-dumping duties were also passed, indicating that the central government had the motivation to implement them early on. Recently, there has been a design for state-operated trade. Then, how can the legitimate initial step of increasing taxes be put aside?

Furthermore, there are numerous precedents for anti-dumping regulations in various countries. For example, Canada repeatedly revised its anti-dumping duties in 1904 and 1907. New Zealand, a small country, also had the Agricultural Implements Manufacturing Import and Implementation Act in 1905. Australia also had two anti-dumping duties. The successive revisions of tariffs in the United States have focused on preventing the dumping of foreign goods. Recently, Germany, France, and many small countries in Central Europe have used tariff protection policies to protect domestic industries from foreign pressure.

Moreover, it is common for countries to impose special tariffs on certain goods. Taking aquatic products as an example, France, in order to protect its domestic sprat fishing industry, used high-pressure tactics against American-made tomato sprats and levied a special aquatic canned food import tax, starting in 1931. For each box of American and Russian goods, the tax was about 16 national currency units, while Canadian goods were taxed at 8 units, and Japanese goods were taxed at only 4 units. Furthermore, Germany considered Japanese canned crab to be a luxury item and levied a special tariff of 18 units per box. Since President Roosevelt took office in the United States, in order to protect domestic aquatic businesses and prevent the dumping of foreign goods, he suddenly announced a protection plan on December 15, 1933. The import taxes on aquatic products were largely increased, and it was stipulated that they would take effect on January 13, 1934. For example, canned tuna imported from foreign countries was subject to a tax of 30% to 45% ad valorem, and oil-soaked sprats priced at less than 9 cents per pound were subject to a tax of 30% to 44% ad valorem. The tax on Japanese-imported bivalve cans was increased to 52% ad valorem from May 31st. Furthermore, New York in the United States, due to the large number of Japanese oyster seedlings being imported (9,000 boxes were shipped in March of the 22nd year (1933), and another 3,000 boxes were shipped in April, showing the large total), specifically prohibited the import of Japanese oyster seedlings from the Pacific coast for transplantation to the Atlantic coast. At the same time, various states on the Pacific coast also followed suit, with a tendency to prohibit imports on the Pacific coast. All of this fully expresses that "any imported aquatic products that harm the domestic fishing industry must have their tariffs increased or be prohibited from import altogether."

If we do not want our aquatic business to sit idly by and wait for death, then we must burn our boats and exhaust every method to "do it"! The best way to "do it" is to implement a quota system for imports under a controlled economy. The import quota system is an important part of modern countries' tariff policies. As a protective tariff policy, this system directly and appropriately restricts the quantity of imports. The method of this system is to determine the total amount of foreign imports by referring to domestic consumption and domestic production, so as not to affect the surplus or deficiency of demand and supply. Furthermore, the implementation of this system does not require special legislation or other legal procedures and is mostly implemented by emergency orders. Currently, our country's tariffs seem to lack absolute freedom due to the constraints of tariff treaties. Like France, which has 72% of its tariffs regulated by commercial treaties, it has often or recently used import quota systems.

The characteristic of the import quota system is that it can adopt equal or proportional quotas for various foreign countries in terms of imports, which is called "external quotas." Currently, Japanese aquatic products are being dumped to such an extent that they are harming our country's fishing industry. We can grant a small amount of import permits or make the quantity equal to the import permits of various countries, so that they cannot manipulate the market. At a minimum, we can know the exact amount and actual price of imports in advance and obtain a control function.

The import quota system should also determine the respective import quantities of domestic importers, which is called "internal quotas." Currently, most of our country's importers import goods blindly, and they especially like to import Japanese goods in order to seek easy profits. Furthermore, they go a step further and repackage the imported Japanese goods in order to sell them off as soon as possible, which promotes the dumping power of Japanese products. The author has always advocated trade control, so this initial control of traders is a point that cannot be ignored.

The import quota system should further determine the import quantity for each month from the total import quantity and should pay more attention to the state of production in domestic industries to stipulate the quantity of certain goods imported in certain months, which is called seasonal quotas. For example, in France, during the one-year period from July 1931 to July 1932, the quantity of general fish prices in October, salted and dried fish in December, and canned fish in February was stipulated, because this is the period of French aquatic production, thereby protecting the industry. As for our country, during the fishing season—such as when large yellow croaker, small yellow croaker, and ribbonfish are abundant in Jiangsu and Zhejiang—most of the production is transported to Shanghai, reaching about 10,000 dan per day, which immediately shows a surplus in the market. Coupled with inconvenient transportation, it is impossible to quickly transport fresh fish out, resulting in low fish prices and suffering for fishermen. However, Japanese fish prices take advantage of this period to intentionally cut prices and dump them, causing chaos in fish prices and the complete collapse of the fishing economy. This period is when a "seasonal tariff" should be implemented. Now, if there is a "seasonal quota" with import restrictions in advance, it will naturally protect domestic industries from foreign pressure.

At this point, we can believe that the import quota system can—and should—be implemented to prevent the dumping of Japanese aquatic products. However, before we implement it, we should have sufficient research. First, we must understand the specific content of the import quota system. Second, we must observe the status of the domestic aquatic economy. Third, we must analyze imported aquatic products! Of course, we should pay special attention to the import status of Japanese products and the domestic production status. Finally, we should grasp the current state of the national economy and the trends of the international economic community.

In addition, the most important preparatory work is to investigate the actual situation of aquatic trade and, more importantly, to obtain accurate import and export statistics. Recently, the National Economic Committee has established an investigation office in Shanghai. The important work has stipulated an item for import and export investigation. We hope that it will pay more attention to aquatic products and have detailed plans. This article cannot discuss it much, but it only hopes that the relevant parties will pay attention to preparing for implementation!

Shanghai News Local Supplement

Talks

Starting from Professional Jealousy 48

— Xin Xin

The matter of professional jealousy, to use a term from the national essence salvation theory, "has existed since ancient times." I remember when I was young, I often heard the saying "competitors are like enemies." And our "businessmen's" forte is nothing more than imitation, counterfeiting, and copying. In this day and age when selfishness is increasingly declining, the reality of professional jealousy will naturally play out more prominently.

I don't know who the clever person was who came up with the method of "professional consensus," trying to use the power of this "professional consensus" to flatten market prices. On the surface, market prices naturally become flat due to discussion, but in reality, it's not like that at all. For example, in silk shops, although the selling price can be the same, the additional markup is at the discretion of the seller. After a long time, the agreed-upon prices become merely a formality.

Someone will definitely blame you for not "agreeing upon" the markup as well. This sounds easy, but in reality, there are still many difficulties. To accommodate customers, the hand naturally loosens a bit. Even if we take a step back and say that everyone is willing to unify without exception, there are still differences in the busyness of the location, the quietness, and the size of the expenses. And the Chinese have a strange temper, stubbornly believing that the older the brand, the better. This can perhaps be refuted with other reasons, but the biggest fatal blow is that if the goods are left for too long, they either spoil or go out of fashion. Taking silk as an example, what used to be three or four yuan per foot for various colorful satins is now worth less than thirty or forty cents per bolt, and no one cares.

Seeing that "procrastination breeds problems," they come up with "professional consensus" again. However, this system that has been negated by objective circumstances has a shorter and shorter "consensus" power each time.

Then, some people rely on strong capital to implement a trust policy. According to the common law of the survival of the fittest, the trust policy naturally has a temporary effect. As a result, the chimneys of nearby factories gradually increase, and handicraftsmen have to abandon their crude tools at home and go to the coal ash conveyor belts to earn a bowl of rice.

However, just as the power of machinery is driving out handicrafts, foreign capital is relying on the various advantages of advanced countries to defeat it. On the one hand, because this change is too fast, and coupled with the various contradictions of capitalism, the Chinese market becomes even more chaotic.

In this chaotic situation, handicraftsmen, on the one hand, have to abandon their crude tools at home, and on the other hand, because the immature industry is killed by foreign capital, they deeply feel that there is no work to do. What's more, they have encountered the raging waves of the world's economic recession, and China has helplessly become the end of the world's dumping ground.

Second- and third-rate shops, under this layer of pressure, cannot resist this irresistible force. To allow it to be swallowed up is naturally unwilling. Before they can clearly identify the target, they spray the poisonous gas of "small profits, high turnover" on their bodies.

But even if they defeat the enemy they currently regard as the enemy, what then? The answer is still not optimistic. Even if we take a step back and say that everyone is putting up the banner of "small profits, high turnover," then the answer is still not optimistic.

If you don't believe it, please look at the facts to prove it later.

One Side of the City 49

— Jing Yun

At 10:30, I came out of the Xinya Restaurant on Nanjing Road. There was no moon in the sky, but there were stars like chess pieces. A few people were a little drunk and dragged their heavy steps.

Although the three major companies and other major stores had closed their doors long ago, another kind of business was actively taking its place. Reflected under the red and bright neon lights of the large glass windows, we could clearly see rows of young women with slicked hair and painted faces standing there, forcing a smile for life, selling their bodies and souls.

——Come on, go to the room to play, come on——

The voice is so touching, melodious, gentle, like a nightingale.

Sending out a charming look, displaying the alluring magic possessed by fox-like women: cotton-like hands, snow-lotus-like arms wrapped around my waist, hugging, pretending to be a very intimate, clinging expression.

Suddenly receiving this unexpected stimulus, I was a little embarrassed, my heart was pounding like a pendulum, and my face was burning a little.

——Haha, Alon, are you carrying good luck today? She's hitting on you...

My friends were laughing, bending over and laughing.

Walking to the intersection of Nanjing Road, the pedestrians and cars were still so crowded. The wind poured down from the top of the large buildings, fresh and cool, blowing away the irritability on my body. At this time, the drunkenness had completely disappeared. Listening to the "toot-toot" whistles of the small steamboats coming and going in the Huangpu River, a few people stood there blankly, a little lost.

Looking at the stars in the sky and the clock tower of the Jianghai Customs, we were speechless and in a daze.

——Where do we go after all?

At this time, everyone's heart seemed to be awakened by the evening breeze, and they realized that they were walking.

——Let's rent a steamboat to take a ride in the center of the river.

——It's better to sit in the Bund Park.

The destination was finally decided, and a few people walked into the gate of the Bund Park one after another.

Although I have been in Shanghai for many years, tonight is my first time entering the Bund Park. What impressed me was that there were so many people, more than any other park. Everywhere you could smell the meaty smell that was both sour and seemed to carry a bit of floral fragrance; and there were many fashionable girls shuttling back and forth like butterflies, displaying her magic to attract the guests in the park.

(A gathering place for sex maniacs, a chasing field; it devours the youth and ambition of young people, and then even throws the shell into the river, letting it flow eastward with the rolling tide.)

It was gradually going away, and the long and short hands of the Jianghai Customs clock had come together and pointed at twelve o'clock. The iron railings along the river had been moistened with a layer of cool dew, and the tourists were also blown very cool and felt a little tired and went home to sleep. However, some pitiful people who could not get customers had to lower their prices to solicit customers for life, struggling desperately in the darkness.

(In fact, looking at it from the outside of the city, it seems so sacred and brilliant; but looking at its dark side, its filth and sin, it will smear the sacredness and brilliance beyond recognition!)

Blood and Sweat 50

— Zhen

This is a fact that I can never forget.

It was the day before I left my hometown, and I happened to think of my kind old uncle, so I decided to go to my uncle's place, partly to relieve boredom and partly to say goodbye.

My uncle was sitting there glumly, picking up his pipe and loading it with tobacco. After I greeted him, I told him that I would be leaving for Shanghai tomorrow.

Suddenly he looked at me in surprise:

"Are you still going to university?"

"Yes." I answered nonchalantly.

Unexpectedly, my uncle shook his head, and from his old and weak eyes, which were failing, were shooting rays of extreme doubt. He put aside his pipe and said to me, "Your university probably costs three or four hundred yuan a year. Oh, this three or four hundred yuan, in our countryside..." My uncle stopped there, sighed deeply, and then continued, "In these years, the price of rice is so cheap, less than six yuan a stone, right? Alas, this three or four hundred yuan, isn't it necessary to exchange six or seventy stones of grain for it?" My uncle deliberately raised his voice. "XX, you must know that these six or seventy stones of grain need the blood and sweat of people, young and old? Let's say that one mu of land can harvest two stones of grain (that's only referring to a good year), then isn't it necessary to harvest from more than thirty mu of land to get six or seventy stones? Alas, how much blood and sweat does it take to irrigate more than thirty mu of land!"

My uncle's words, one sound after another, were piercing my heart like a drill. Yes. Drop by drop of blood and sweat, working tirelessly year after year, the families on more than thirty mu of land, selling all their grain, can only barely provide for the expenses of one university student. I was so moved that I sat there motionless. I had no words to respond. I felt deeply ashamed. Did I have such a right? Could I be so callous? Alas! I alone was absorbing such an immeasurable amount of other people's blood and sweat. At the same time, a shocking tragedy floated before my eyes: I seemed to see batches of cash, transformed from the blood and sweat of the countryside, being brought into the city by many young men and women, who completely forgot that this silver was inlaid with the blood and sweat of farmers, and handed it over one by one to the bosses of theaters, the bosses of dance halls... My head was dizzy, and my eyes seemed to be filled with piles of blood, stones of grain. "Uncle, goodbye." I couldn't sit there any longer.

Talking About the Mouth 51

— Bin

The mouth is the tool for eating, and also the tool for talking. Because it can eat and talk, we are turned upside down and rushing around between this in and out, and it has to talk about itself.

Because the words it speaks are humble, it is inevitably scolded for flattering; the words it speaks are arrogant, and it is even more inevitably scolded for boasting; the words it speaks are harsh, and it will be resented; the words it speaks are soft, and it will be said to be useless. If it's too straightforward, it will offend people; if it's too cunning, it will be deceiving. If it's too honest, it will be fooled; if it's too hypocritical, it will lose credibility. If it doesn't talk when it should talk, it's called not being able to talk; if it talks when it shouldn't, it will be rebuffed. We are left with this not good, that not good, it is really hateful.

Furthermore, talking about its eating is even more endless. Three meals a day, eating today, eating tomorrow, eating the day after tomorrow, never resting (except when there is a reason to rest). One day, but I have never seen it full. Moreover, in this era when there are more monks than congee, rice is the most difficult to get. You must have the ability to find food. Otherwise, when people cook fragrant white rice and delicious delicacies, we can only swallow our saliva towards our stomachs, watching it not being able to eat. Even if we are lucky and find a rice bowl, damn it, there is no meal provided, and we still have to bother ourselves to find food. Especially, when it comes to flavorful foods, it is not polite at all, it just chews; tasteless, or foods with a slightly unpleasant taste, hand it to it, sorry, it will immediately be unhappy, and even frown. Don't you think it is the number one villain in the world?

From this point of view, it treats us people as slaves, like Tang Seng, who put the golden ring on Sun Wukong's head, so that we can't get rid of it.

Gao Fushou 52

— Village Cause

Gao Fushou always came home drunk and boisterous.

His face, his eyes… like a beaten-down, dying lion! He seemed to have boundless grievances, as if he wanted to roar out from his chest, but something always suppressed it.

He often said to people:

— Drinking can help me avoid being entangled by many hideous faces!

His words were a bit incomprehensible! Because an executioner wouldn't be afraid of anything!

— Old Gao! You're used to killing people. Are you afraid of these things?

Upon hearing this, Gao Fushou was stunned, and said painfully and heavily:

— Sir! You don't understand. I believe: there isn't anyone in the world who truly wants to do the job of killing!

— Old Gao! Then why do you do this job of killing?

— Ah! Sir. Who doesn't want to quit this profession! But if I quit, where will I find food to feed my family of five?

His eyeballs were filled with red veins! His hairy hand kept clenching. He said.

— How many people have you killed?

This question made him even more uneasy! Slowly, he said reluctantly:

— Sir! In total, I have killed…

He paused, his eyes fixed, calculating. Then he continued:

— In total, I have killed more than thirty people! Some were hanged, some were beheaded, some were shot! … Hmm. Sir! You don't know about those who were hanged! … They… If I think about it carefully! I simply don't want to see this world anymore! This world… Sir! Goodbye!

With that, he grabbed his head and ran away like a madman!

On the street, the others who saw him in this state laughed. One of them said to me:

— He is not a sinner!

— No, he is doing good deeds for his children! Because all the people he killed were bad people…

These words, one by one, were transmitted into my ears.

About five months later, rumors spread on the street:

! Gao Fushou is dead!

! It's right that an executioner should die like this!

! Hmm. I heard that he went crazy and gouged out his own eyes! Then he bit off all ten of his fingers! Shouting madly: "I don't want to see this world anymore! I don't want to use these hands to do this anymore!"

! How did he die later?

! Later, later he died in pain!

Five days after his death, I ran into his wife.

— Sir! Please give me some help!

At first, I didn't recognize her as Gao Fushou's wife, but then she said herself:

— Sir! Please have pity on me! My husband recently went mad and died! Leaving behind, there is an old mother, and three young children… According to the officials in the yamen, I should be able to get twenty dollars in compensation! But I only got five dollars… To this day, I still can't afford to bury him! I have no money! Sir. Ah! He already smells… Please have some compassion…

Hearing her words, I reached into my pocket to find money. Heavens! I only had one round silver dollar! I gave it all to her! In this way, I went hungry for three days!

Look: The bleak snow, buries many

Gao Fushou's death, almost everywhere is wearing white mourning clothes! However, once the sun comes out, these will turn into water!…

The Whip of Life 53

— Simon

The accumulation of days cruelly plundered everything, pushing me from childhood into the hell of adulthood, so I had to start chewing on the bitter plans of life. I have a young body and an old heart. Everything in front of me is covered with a layer of grayness, not a bit of excitement arises in me, but only fatigue, boundless fatigue and boundless sorrow.

"What else do I hope for?" Facing the cold, ruthless face of life presented before me, I often asked myself with a touch of hysteria. Yes, who says the upper side of life is painted with blue color, a picture of longing. These beautiful lines have never floated in my mind, nor have I ever planted the idea of fantasy in it. I only know that life to me is simply a failing leather whip, flogging my back every day. I have simply become a camel, become a cart, carrying stones and coal weighing a thousand pounds, driven by the whip of life, gasping for breath, sweating, walking on the confusing, endless, dark night road, there is no moon in the sky, nor houses, no thick shadows surround me, I will forever be in the trembling shadows, carrying heavy burdens and crawling forward.

In this way, I gradually became thin, so thin that only an empty shell of skin and bones remained. And the whip of life still does not let up on grinding me. I wanted to rest for a moment, but it always shouted at me to hurry on the road, I had nothing to say, I could only grit my teeth and listen to it continue to ravage me; in this way, I almost lost even my senses, do I still believe that I am a person with a soul! I am almost the same as a soulless yin corpse!

The dust swept up by the road of life, layer upon layer, pressed down on my thoughts. Buried my eyes, I can't see everything, I only see the vastness of the sea, the melancholy sky. Besides being the cattle and horses of life, suffering every day, what else have I gained! I often open my eyes in the sleepless late night, grab my own hair; desperately beat my chest, even forget the pain and hit the wall with my hands, constantly shouting, "What can life give me after all," but life doesn't pay attention to me, its mouth always hangs with a vicious sneer, and when tomorrow comes, life comes again to force me, pulling me to squeeze into that big millstone to grind and break, so I endure the pain and struggle, and struggle day by day, ah! My autumn leaf-like body, I really can't support it anymore, I am ready to use the last of my remaining life to fight life to the death, but I don't have a shred of strength, I can only watch the demon of life devour my flesh in one mouthful ah! …

Nicknames 54

— Ryunosuke Akutagawa, translated by Wakagi

Nicknames, like works of art, can reveal a person's personality. Like Hishida Shunso, in his youth he was called "Swift Runner". So Shunso in his youth was probably very "swift". If that's not wrong, then Masamune Hakucho should have been called Shirotsuka in his youth. -- Whether he was called Shirotsuka, perhaps my memory is wrong, but, assuming it's not wrong, then from this nickname, it is enough to infer Masamune Hakucho in his youth. Therefore, I think that ancient literati shouldered many nicknames, not treating nicknames like amusing toys, but adapting to the progress of their interests. (Chengjiangtang Miscellany)

Self-Cultivation

Conscience is a kind of serious taste.

Conscience may have created morality, but morality has not created the "good" character of conscience.

Conscience is like taste, it has a morbidly compassionate component. However, among those who are morbidly compassionate, eight or nine out of ten are smart, aristocratic, and wealthy, these kinds of people. (Dwarf's Words)

Busy

What can rescue us from the poisonous thickets of love: busyness is even more powerful than reason. To practice love, time is more important than anything. Like Werther, Romeo, Tolstoy, etc., who are called ancient saints of love, they are all idle people. (Ibid.)

Men

From ancient times, men have always regarded their careers as more important and more respectable than love. If you doubt that this is not the truth, then please read Balzac's letters. Balzac wrote to Mrs. Hanska, "This letter, if put up for auction, will get a lot of francs in royalties." (Ibid.)

Confession

The ancients confessed before God; people today confess before society. Because no matter who, no matter what it is -- except for fools, and evildoers are exceptions -- if they don't confess, they may feel very painful at present.

Also

Although no matter how they confess, whether they can gain that kind of trust is their own business, and at the same time it becomes another question. (Ibid.)
